| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchExpressions**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecEgressItems0ToRequiresItems0MatchExpressionsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecegressitems0torequiresitems0matchexpressionsitems0)]|matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecEgressItems0ToRequiresItems0MatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecEnableDefaultDeny

EnableDefaultDeny determines whether this policy configures the subject endpoint(s) to have a default deny mode. If enabled, this causes all traffic not explicitly allowed by a network policy to be dropped. If not specified, the default is true for each traffic direction that has rules, and false otherwise. For example, if a policy only has Ingress or IngressDeny rules, then the default for ingress is true and egress is false. If multiple policies apply to an endpoint, that endpoint&#39;s default deny will be enabled if any policy requests it. This is useful for creating broad-based network policies that will not cause endpoints to enter default-deny mode.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**egress**|bool|Whether or not the endpoint should have a default-deny rule applied to egress traffic.||
|**ingress**|bool|Whether or not the endpoint should have a default-deny rule applied to ingress traffic.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecEndpointSelector

EndpointSelector selects all endpoints which should be subject to this rule. EndpointSelector and NodeSelector cannot be both empty and are mutually exclusive.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||

|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0

IngressDenyRule contains all rule types which can be applied at ingress, i.e. network traffic that originates outside of the endpoint and is entering the endpoint selected by the endpointSelector. - All members of this structure are optional. If omitted or empty, the member will have no effect on the rule. - If multiple members are set, all of them need to match in order for the rule to take effect. The exception to this rule is FromRequires field; the effects of any Requires field in any rule will apply to all other rules as well. - FromEndpoints, FromCIDR, FromCIDRSet, FromGroups and FromEntities are mutually exclusive. Only one of these members may be present within an individual rule.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**fromCIDR**|[str]|FromCIDR is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from. Only connections which do *not* originate from the cluster or from the local host are subject to CIDR rules. In order to allow in-cluster connectivity, use the FromEndpoints field.  This will match on the source IP address of incoming connections. Adding  a prefix into FromCIDR or into FromCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is  equivalent.  Overlaps are allowed between FromCIDR and FromCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=my-legacy-pet" is allowed to receive connections from 10.3.9.1||
|**fromCIDRSet**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromCIDRSetItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0fromcidrsetitems0)]|FromCIDRSet is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from in addition to FromEndpoints, along with a list of subnets contained within their corresponding IP block from which traffic should not be allowed. This will match on the source IP address of incoming connections. Adding a prefix into FromCIDR or into FromCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. Overlaps are allowed between FromCIDR and FromCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=my-legacy-pet" is allowed to receive connections from 10.0.0.0/8 except from IPs in subnet 10.96.0.0/12.||
|**fromEndpoints**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromEndpointsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0fromendpointsitems0)]|FromEndpoints is a list of endpoints identified by an EndpointSelector which are allowed to communicate with the endpoint subject to the rule.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=backend" can be consumed by any endpoint carrying the label "role=frontend".||
|**fromEntities**|[str]|FromEntities is a list of special entities which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from. Supported entities are `world`, `cluster` and `host`||
|**fromGroups**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromGroupsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0fromgroupsitems0)]|FromGroups is a directive that allows the integration with multiple outside providers. Currently, only AWS is supported, and the rule can select by multiple sub directives:<br />Example: FromGroups: - aws: securityGroupsIds: - &#39;sg-XXXXXXXXXXXXX&#39;||
|**fromNodes**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromNodesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0fromnodesitems0)]|FromNodes is a list of nodes identified by an EndpointSelector which are allowed to communicate with the endpoint subject to the rule.||
|**fromRequires**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromRequiresItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0fromrequiresitems0)]|FromRequires is a list of additional constraints which must be met in order for the selected endpoints to be reachable. These additional constraints do no by itself grant access privileges and must always be accompanied with at least one matching FromEndpoints.<br />Example: Any Endpoint with the label "team=A" requires consuming endpoint to also carry the label "team=A".||
|**icmps**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0icmpsitems0)]|ICMPs is a list of ICMP rule identified by type number which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can not accept incoming type 8 ICMP connections.||
|**toPorts**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0ToPortsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressdenyitems0toportsitems0)]|ToPorts is a list of destination ports identified by port number and protocol which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can not accept incoming connections on port 80/tcp.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressDenyItems0FromCIDRSetItems0

CIDRRule is a rule that specifies a CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication  is allowed, along with an optional list of subnets within that CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication is not allowed.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidr**|str|CIDR is a CIDR prefix / IP Block.||
|**cidrGroupRef**|str|CIDRGroupRef is a reference to a CiliumCIDRGroup object. A CiliumCIDRGroup contains a list of CIDRs that the endpoint, subject to the rule, can (Ingress/Egress) or cannot (IngressDeny/EgressDeny) receive connections from.||
|**except**|[str]|ExceptCIDRs is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to initiate connections to. These CIDR prefixes should be contained within Cidr, using ExceptCIDRs together with CIDRGroupRef is not supported yet. These exceptions are only applied to the Cidr in this CIDRRule, and do not apply to any other CIDR prefixes in any other CIDRRules.||

|**fromEntities**|[str]|FromEntities is a list of special entities which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from. Supported entities are `world`, `cluster` and `host`||
|**fromGroups**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0FromGroupsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0fromgroupsitems0)]|FromGroups is a directive that allows the integration with multiple outside providers. Currently, only AWS is supported, and the rule can select by multiple sub directives:<br />Example: FromGroups: - aws: securityGroupsIds: - &#39;sg-XXXXXXXXXXXXX&#39;||
|**fromNodes**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0FromNodesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0fromnodesitems0)]|FromNodes is a list of nodes identified by an EndpointSelector which are allowed to communicate with the endpoint subject to the rule.||
|**fromRequires**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0FromRequiresItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0fromrequiresitems0)]|FromRequires is a list of additional constraints which must be met in order for the selected endpoints to be reachable. These additional constraints do no by itself grant access privileges and must always be accompanied with at least one matching FromEndpoints.<br />Example: Any Endpoint with the label "team=A" requires consuming endpoint to also carry the label "team=A".||
|**icmps**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0IcmpsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0icmpsitems0)]|ICMPs is a list of ICMP rule identified by type number which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can only accept incoming type 8 ICMP connections.||
|**toPorts**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0toportsitems0)]|ToPorts is a list of destination ports identified by port number and protocol which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can only accept incoming connections on port 80/tcp.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0FromCIDRSetItems0

CIDRRule is a rule that specifies a CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication  is allowed, along with an optional list of subnets within that CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication is not allowed.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidr**|str|CIDR is a CIDR prefix / IP Block.||
|**cidrGroupRef**|str|CIDRGroupRef is a reference to a CiliumCIDRGroup object. A CiliumCIDRGroup contains a list of CIDRs that the endpoint, subject to the rule, can (Ingress/Egress) or cannot (IngressDeny/EgressDeny) receive connections from.||
|**except**|[str]|ExceptCIDRs is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to initiate connections to. These CIDR prefixes should be contained within Cidr, using ExceptCIDRs together with CIDRGroupRef is not supported yet. These exceptions are only applied to the Cidr in this CIDRRule, and do not apply to any other CIDR prefixes in any other CIDRRules.||

|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0FromEndpointsItems0MatchExpressionsItems0

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLS

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLSSecret

Secret is the secret that contains the certificates and private key for the TLS context. By default, Cilium will search in this secret for the following items: - &#39;ca.crt&#39;  - Which represents the trusted CA to verify remote source. - &#39;tls.crt&#39; - Which represents the public key certificate. - &#39;tls.key&#39; - Which represents the private key matching the public key certificate.

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesDNSItems0

PortRuleDNS is a list of allowed DNS lookups.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchName**|str|MatchName matches literal DNS names. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.||
|**matchPattern**|str|MatchPattern allows using wildcards to match DNS names. All wildcards are case insensitive. The wildcards are: - "*" matches 0 or more DNS valid characters, and may occur anywhere in the pattern. As a special case a "*" as the leftmost character, without a following "." matches all subdomains as well as the name to the right. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.<br />Examples: `*.cilium.io` matches subomains of cilium at that level www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io match, cilium.io and google.com do not `*cilium.io` matches cilium.io and all subdomains ends with "cilium.io" except those containing "." separator, subcilium.io and sub-cilium.io match, www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io does not sub*.cilium.io matches subdomains of cilium where the subdomain component begins with "sub" sub.cilium.io and subdomain.cilium.io match, www.cilium.io, blog.cilium.io, cilium.io and google.com do not||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0

PortRuleHTTP is a list of HTTP protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule does not have any effect. All fields of this type are extended POSIX regex as defined by IEEE Std 1003.1, (i.e this follows the egrep/unix syntax, not the perl syntax) matched against the path of an incoming request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**headerMatches**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0)]|HeaderMatches is a list of HTTP headers which must be present and match against the given values. Mismatch field can be used to specify what to do when there is no match.||
|**headers**|[str]|Headers is a list of HTTP headers which must be present in the request. If omitted or empty, requests are allowed regardless of headers present.||
|**host**|str|Host is an extended POSIX regex matched against the host header of a request, e.g. "foo.com"<br />If omitted or empty, the value of the host header is ignored.||
|**method**|str|Method is an extended POSIX regex matched against the method of a request, e.g. "GET", "POST", "PUT", "PATCH", "DELETE", ...<br />If omitted or empty, all methods are allowed.||
|**path**|str|Path is an extended POSIX regex matched against the path of a request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.<br />If omitted or empty, all paths are all allowed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0

HeaderMatch extends the HeaderValue for matching requirement of a named header field against an immediate string, a secret value, or a regex.  If none of the optional fields is present, then the header value is not matched, only presence of the header is enough.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**mismatch**|"LOG" \| "ADD" \| "DELETE" \| "REPLACE"|Mismatch identifies what to do in case there is no match. The default is to drop the request. Otherwise the overall rule is still considered as matching, but the mismatches are logged in the access log.||
|**name** `required`|str|Name identifies the header.||
|**secret**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0secret)|secret||
|**value**|str|Value matches the exact value of the header. Can be specified either alone or together with "Secret"; will be used as the header value if the secret can not be found in the latter case.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret

Secret refers to a secret that contains the value to be matched against. The secret must only contain one entry. If the referred secret does not exist, and there is no "Value" specified, the match will fail.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**name** `required`|str|Name is the name of the secret.||
|**namespace**|str|Namespace is the namespace in which the secret exists. Context of use determines the default value if left out (e.g., "default").||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesKafkaItems0

PortRule is a list of Kafka protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule will match all Kafka messages.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**apiKey**|str|APIKey is a case-insensitive string matched against the key of a request, e.g. "produce", "fetch", "createtopic", "deletetopic", et al Reference: https://kafka.apache.org/protocol#protocol_api_keys<br />If omitted or empty, and if Role is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**apiVersion**|str|APIVersion is the version matched against the api version of the Kafka message. If set, it has to be a string representing a positive integer.<br />If omitted or empty, all versions are allowed.||
|**clientID**|str|ClientID is the client identifier as provided in the request.<br />From Kafka protocol documentation: This is a user supplied identifier for the client application. The user can use any identifier they like and it will be used when logging errors, monitoring aggregates, etc. For example, one might want to monitor not just the requests per second overall, but the number coming from each client application (each of which could reside on multiple servers). This id acts as a logical grouping across all requests from a particular client.<br />If omitted or empty, all client identifiers are allowed.||
|**role**|"produce" \| "consume"|Role is a case-insensitive string and describes a group of API keys necessary to perform certain higher-level Kafka operations such as "produce" or "consume". A Role automatically expands into all APIKeys required to perform the specified higher-level operation.<br />The following values are supported: - "produce": Allow producing to the topics specified in the rule - "consume": Allow consuming from the topics specified in the rule<br />This field is incompatible with the APIKey field, i.e APIKey and Role cannot both be specified in the same rule.<br />If omitted or empty, and if APIKey is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**topic**|str|Topic is the topic name contained in the message. If a Kafka request contains multiple topics, then all topics must be allowed or the message will be rejected.<br />This constraint is ignored if the matched request message type doesn&#39;t contain any topic. Maximum size of Topic can be 249 characters as per recent Kafka spec and allowed characters are a-z, A-Z, 0-9, -, . and _.<br />Older Kafka versions had longer topic lengths of 255, but in Kafka 0.10 version the length was changed from 255 to 249. For compatibility reasons we are using 255.<br />If omitted or empty, all topics are allowed.||

For ingress policy this specifies the server-side TLS parameters to be applied on the connections originated from a remote source and terminated by the L7 proxy.

|**privateKey**|str|PrivateKey is the file name or k8s secret item name for the private key matching the certificate chain. If omitted, &#39;tls.key&#39; is assumed, if it exists. If given, the item must exist.||
|**secret** `required`|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecIngressItems0ToPortsItems0TerminatingTLSSecret](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecingressitems0toportsitems0terminatingtlssecret)|secret||
|**trustedCA**|str|TrustedCA is the file name or k8s secret item name for the trusted CA. If omitted, &#39;ca.crt&#39; is assumed, if it exists. If given, the item must exist.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0

Rule is a policy rule which must be applied to all endpoints which match the labels contained in the endpointSelector Each rule is split into an ingress section which contains all rules applicable at ingress, and an egress section applicable at egress. For rule types such as `L4Rule` and `CIDR` which can be applied at both ingress and egress, both ingress and egress side have to either specifically allow the connection or one side has to be omitted. Either ingress, egress, or both can be provided. If both ingress and egress are omitted, the rule has no effect.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**description**|str|Description is a free form string, it can be used by the creator of the rule to store human readable explanation of the purpose of this rule. Rules cannot be identified by comment.||
|**egress**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0)]|Egress is a list of EgressRule which are enforced at egress. If omitted or empty, this rule does not apply at egress.||
|**egressDeny**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0)]|EgressDeny is a list of EgressDenyRule which are enforced at egress. Any rule inserted here will be denied regardless of the allowed egress rules in the &#39;egress&#39; field. If omitted or empty, this rule does not apply at egress.||
|**enableDefaultDeny**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EnableDefaultDeny](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0enabledefaultdeny)|enable default deny||
|**endpointSelector**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EndpointSelector](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0endpointselector)|endpoint selector||
|**ingress**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressitems0)]|Ingress is a list of IngressRule which are enforced at ingress. If omitted or empty, this rule does not apply at ingress.||
|**ingressDeny**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0)]|IngressDeny is a list of IngressDenyRule which are enforced at ingress. Any rule inserted here will be denied regardless of the allowed ingress rules in the &#39;ingress&#39; field. If omitted or empty, this rule does not apply at ingress.||
|**labels**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0LabelsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0labelsitems0)]|Labels is a list of optional strings which can be used to re-identify the rule or to store metadata. It is possible to lookup or delete strings based on labels. Labels are not required to be unique, multiple rules can have overlapping or identical labels.||
|**nodeSelector**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0NodeSelector](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0nodeselector)|node selector||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0

EgressDenyRule contains all rule types which can be applied at egress, i.e. network traffic that originates inside the endpoint and exits the endpoint selected by the endpointSelector. - All members of this structure are optional. If omitted or empty, the member will have no effect on the rule. - If multiple members of the structure are specified, then all members must match in order for the rule to take effect. The exception to this rule is the ToRequires member; the effects of any Requires field in any rule will apply to all other rules as well. - ToEndpoints, ToCIDR, ToCIDRSet, ToEntities, ToServices and ToGroups are mutually exclusive. Only one of these members may be present within an individual rule.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**icmps**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0icmpsitems0)]|ICMPs is a list of ICMP rule identified by type number which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to connect to.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" is not allowed to initiate type 8 ICMP connections.||
|**toCIDR**|[str]|ToCIDR is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections. Only connections destined for outside of the cluster and not targeting the host will be subject to CIDR rules.  This will match on the destination IP address of outgoing connections. Adding a prefix into ToCIDR or into ToCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. Overlaps are allowed between ToCIDR and ToCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=database-proxy" is allowed to initiate connections to 10.2.3.0/24||
|**toCIDRSet**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToCIDRSetItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0tocidrsetitems0)]|ToCIDRSet is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections to in addition to connections which are allowed via ToEndpoints, along with a list of subnets contained within their corresponding IP block to which traffic should not be allowed. This will match on the destination IP address of outgoing connections. Adding a prefix into ToCIDR or into ToCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. Overlaps are allowed between ToCIDR and ToCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=database-proxy" is allowed to initiate connections to 10.2.3.0/24 except from IPs in subnet 10.2.3.0/28.||
|**toEndpoints**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToEndpointsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0toendpointsitems0)]|ToEndpoints is a list of endpoints identified by an EndpointSelector to which the endpoints subject to the rule are allowed to communicate.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=frontend" can communicate with any endpoint carrying the label "role=backend".||
|**toEntities**|[str]|ToEntities is a list of special entities to which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections. Supported entities are `world`, `cluster`,`host`,`remote-node`,`kube-apiserver`, `init`, `health`,`unmanaged` and `all`.||
|**toGroups**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToGroupsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0togroupsitems0)]|ToGroups is a directive that allows the integration with multiple outside providers. Currently, only AWS is supported, and the rule can select by multiple sub directives:<br />Example: toGroups: - aws: securityGroupsIds: - &#39;sg-XXXXXXXXXXXXX&#39;||
|**toNodes**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToNodesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0tonodesitems0)]|ToNodes is a list of nodes identified by an EndpointSelector to which endpoints subject to the rule is allowed to communicate.||
|**toPorts**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToPortsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0toportsitems0)]|ToPorts is a list of destination ports identified by port number and protocol which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to connect to.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=frontend" is not allowed to initiate connections to destination port 8080/tcp||
|**toRequires**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToRequiresItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0torequiresitems0)]|ToRequires is a list of additional constraints which must be met in order for the selected endpoints to be able to connect to other endpoints. These additional constraints do no by itself grant access privileges and must always be accompanied with at least one matching ToEndpoints.<br />Example: Any Endpoint with the label "team=A" requires any endpoint to which it communicates to also carry the label "team=A".||
|**toServices**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToServicesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0toservicesitems0)]|ToServices is a list of services to which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections. Currently Cilium only supports toServices for K8s services without selectors.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=backend-app" is allowed to initiate connections to all cidrs backing the "external-service" service||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0

ICMPRule is a list of ICMP fields.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**fields**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0FieldsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0icmpsitems0fieldsitems0)]|Fields is a list of ICMP fields.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0FieldsItems0

ICMPField is a ICMP field.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**family**|"IPv4" \| "IPv6"|Family is a IP address version. Currently, we support `IPv4` and `IPv6`. `IPv4` is set as default.|"IPv4"|
|**type** `required`|int \| str|||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToCIDRSetItems0

CIDRRule is a rule that specifies a CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication  is allowed, along with an optional list of subnets within that CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication is not allowed.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidr**|str|CIDR is a CIDR prefix / IP Block.||
|**cidrGroupRef**|str|CIDRGroupRef is a reference to a CiliumCIDRGroup object. A CiliumCIDRGroup contains a list of CIDRs that the endpoint, subject to the rule, can (Ingress/Egress) or cannot (IngressDeny/EgressDeny) receive connections from.||
|**except**|[str]|ExceptCIDRs is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to initiate connections to. These CIDR prefixes should be contained within Cidr, using ExceptCIDRs together with CIDRGroupRef is not supported yet. These exceptions are only applied to the Cidr in this CIDRRule, and do not apply to any other CIDR prefixes in any other CIDRRules.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToEndpointsItems0

EndpointSelector is a wrapper for k8s LabelSelector.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchExpressions**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToEndpointsItems0MatchExpressionsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressdenyitems0toendpointsitems0matchexpressionsitems0)]|matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressDenyItems0ToEndpointsItems0MatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0

EgressRule contains all rule types which can be applied at egress, i.e. network traffic that originates inside the endpoint and exits the endpoint selected by the endpointSelector. - All members of this structure are optional. If omitted or empty, the member will have no effect on the rule. - If multiple members of the structure are specified, then all members must match in order for the rule to take effect. The exception to this rule is the ToRequires member; the effects of any Requires field in any rule will apply to all other rules as well. - ToEndpoints, ToCIDR, ToCIDRSet, ToEntities, ToServices and ToGroups are mutually exclusive. Only one of these members may be present within an individual rule.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**authentication**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0Authentication](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0authentication)|authentication||
|**icmps**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0IcmpsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0icmpsitems0)]|ICMPs is a list of ICMP rule identified by type number which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to connect to.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" is allowed to initiate type 8 ICMP connections.||

Adding a prefix into ToCIDR or into ToCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. Overlaps are allowed between ToCIDR and ToCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=database-proxy" is allowed to initiate connections to 10.2.3.0/24||
|**toCIDRSet**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToCIDRSetItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0tocidrsetitems0)]|ToCIDRSet is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections to in addition to connections which are allowed via ToEndpoints, along with a list of subnets contained within their corresponding IP block to which traffic should not be allowed. This will match on the destination IP address of outgoing connections. Adding a prefix into ToCIDR or into ToCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. |**toEndpoints**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToEndpointsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toendpointsitems0)]|ToEndpoints is a list of endpoints identified by an EndpointSelector to which the endpoints subject to the rule are allowed to communicate.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=frontend" can communicate with any endpoint carrying the label "role=backend".||
|**toEntities**|[str]|ToEntities is a list of special entities to which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections. Supported entities are `world`, `cluster`,`host`,`remote-node`,`kube-apiserver`, `init`, `health`,`unmanaged` and `all`.||
|**toFQDNs**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToFQDNsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0tofqdnsitems0)]|ToFQDN allows whitelisting DNS names in place of IPs. The IPs that result from DNS resolution of `ToFQDN.MatchName`s are added to the same EgressRule object as ToCIDRSet entries, and behave accordingly. Any L4 and L7 rules within this EgressRule will also apply to these IPs. The DNS -&gt; IP mapping is re-resolved periodically from within the cilium-agent, and the IPs in the DNS response are effected in the policy for selected pods as-is (i.e. the list of IPs is not modified in any way). Note: An explicit rule to allow for DNS traffic is needed for the pods, as ToFQDN counts as an egress rule and will enforce egress policy when PolicyEnforcment=default. Note: If the resolved IPs are IPs within the kubernetes cluster, the ToFQDN rule will not apply to that IP. Note: ToFQDN cannot occur in the same policy as other To* rules.||
|**toGroups**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToGroupsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0togroupsitems0)]|ToGroups is a directive that allows the integration with multiple outside providers. Currently, only AWS is supported, and the rule can select by multiple sub directives:<br />Example: toGroups: - aws: securityGroupsIds: - &#39;sg-XXXXXXXXXXXXX&#39;||
|**toNodes**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToNodesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0tonodesitems0)]|ToNodes is a list of nodes identified by an EndpointSelector to which endpoints subject to the rule is allowed to communicate.||
|**toPorts**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toportsitems0)]|ToPorts is a list of destination ports identified by port number and protocol which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to connect to.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=frontend" is allowed to initiate connections to destination port 8080/tcp||
|**toRequires**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToRequiresItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0torequiresitems0)]|ToRequires is a list of additional constraints which must be met in order for the selected endpoints to be able to connect to other endpoints. These additional constraints do no by itself grant access privileges and must always be accompanied with at least one matching ToEndpoints.<br />Example: Any Endpoint with the label "team=A" requires any endpoint to which it communicates to also carry the label "team=A".||
|**toServices**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToServicesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toservicesitems0)]|ToServices is a list of services to which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to initiate connections. ### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0IcmpsItems0

#### Attributes

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToCIDRSetItems0

CIDRRule is a rule that specifies a CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication  is allowed, along with an optional list of subnets within that CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication is not allowed.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidr**|str|CIDR is a CIDR prefix / IP Block.||
|**cidrGroupRef**|str|CIDRGroupRef is a reference to a CiliumCIDRGroup object. A CiliumCIDRGroup contains a list of CIDRs that the endpoint, subject to the rule, can (Ingress/Egress) or cannot (IngressDeny/EgressDeny) receive connections from.||
|**except**|[str]|ExceptCIDRs is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to initiate connections to. These CIDR prefixes should be contained within Cidr, using ExceptCIDRs together with CIDRGroupRef is not supported yet. These exceptions are only applied to the Cidr in this CIDRRule, and do not apply to any other CIDR prefixes in any other CIDRRules.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToEndpointsItems0MatchExpressionsItems0

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToFQDNsItems0

cilium io v2 cilium network policy specs items0 egress items0 to f q d ns items0

| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchName**|str|MatchName matches literal DNS names. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.||
|**matchPattern**|str|MatchPattern allows using wildcards to match DNS names. All wildcards are case insensitive. The wildcards are: - "*" matches 0 or more DNS valid characters, and may occur anywhere in the pattern. As a special case a "*" as the leftmost character, without a following "." matches all subdomains as well as the name to the right. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.<br />Examples: `*.cilium.io` matches subomains of cilium at that level www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io match, cilium.io and google.com do not `*cilium.io` matches cilium.io and all subdomains ends with "cilium.io" except those containing "." separator, subcilium.io and sub-cilium.io match, www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io does not sub*.cilium.io matches subdomains of cilium where the subdomain component begins with "sub" sub.cilium.io and subdomain.cilium.io match, www.cilium.io, blog.cilium.io, cilium.io and google.com do not||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLS

OriginatingTLS is the TLS context for the connections originated by the L7 proxy.  For egress policy this specifies the client-side TLS parameters for the upstream connection originating from the L7 proxy to the remote destination. For ingress policy this specifies the client-side TLS parameters for the connection from the L7 proxy to the local endpoint.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**certificate**|str|Certificate is the file name or k8s secret item name for the certificate chain. If omitted, &#39;tls.crt&#39; is assumed, if it exists. If given, the item must exist.||
|**privateKey**|str|PrivateKey is the file name or k8s secret item name for the private key matching the certificate chain. If omitted, &#39;tls.key&#39; is assumed, if it exists. If given, the item must exist.||
|**secret** `required`|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLSSecret](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toportsitems0originatingtlssecret)|secret||
|**trustedCA**|str|TrustedCA is the file name or k8s secret item name for the trusted CA. If omitted, &#39;ca.crt&#39; is assumed, if it exists. If given, the item must exist.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLSSecret

Secret is the secret that contains the certificates and private key for the TLS context. By default, Cilium will search in this secret for the following items: - &#39;ca.crt&#39;  - Which represents the trusted CA to verify remote source. - &#39;tls.crt&#39; - Which represents the public key certificate. - &#39;tls.key&#39; - Which represents the private key matching the public key certificate.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**name** `required`|str|Name is the name of the secret.||
|**namespace**|str|Namespace is the namespace in which the secret exists. Context of use determines the default value if left out (e.g., "default").||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0

PortRuleHTTP is a list of HTTP protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule does not have any effect. All fields of this type are extended POSIX regex as defined by IEEE Std 1003.1, (i.e this follows the egrep/unix syntax, not the perl syntax) matched against the path of an incoming request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**headerMatches**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0)]|HeaderMatches is a list of HTTP headers which must be present and match against the given values. Mismatch field can be used to specify what to do when there is no match.||
|**headers**|[str]|Headers is a list of HTTP headers which must be present in the request. If omitted or empty, requests are allowed regardless of headers present.||
|**host**|str|Host is an extended POSIX regex matched against the host header of a request, e.g. "foo.com"<br />If omitted or empty, the value of the host header is ignored.||
|**method**|str|Method is an extended POSIX regex matched against the method of a request, e.g. "GET", "POST", "PUT", "PATCH", "DELETE", ...<br />If omitted or empty, all methods are allowed.||
|**path**|str|Path is an extended POSIX regex matched against the path of a request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.<br />If omitted or empty, all paths are all allowed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0

HeaderMatch extends the HeaderValue for matching requirement of a named header field against an immediate string, a secret value, or a regex.  If none of the optional fields is present, then the header value is not matched, only presence of the header is enough.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**mismatch**|"LOG" \| "ADD" \| "DELETE" \| "REPLACE"|Mismatch identifies what to do in case there is no match. The default is to drop the request. Otherwise the overall rule is still considered as matching, but the mismatches are logged in the access log.||
|**name** `required`|str|Name identifies the header.||
|**secret**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0egressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0secret)|secret||
|**value**|str|Value matches the exact value of the header. Can be specified either alone or together with "Secret"; will be used as the header value if the secret can not be found in the latter case.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret

Secret refers to a secret that contains the value to be matched against. The secret must only contain one entry. If the referred secret does not exist, and there is no "Value" specified, the match will fail.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**name** `required`|str|Name is the name of the secret.||
|**namespace**|str|Namespace is the namespace in which the secret exists. Context of use determines the default value if left out (e.g., "default").||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EgressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesKafkaItems0

PortRule is a list of Kafka protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule will match all Kafka messages.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**apiKey**|str|APIKey is a case-insensitive string matched against the key of a request, e.g. "produce", "fetch", "createtopic", "deletetopic", et al Reference: https://kafka.apache.org/protocol#protocol_api_keys<br />If omitted or empty, and if Role is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**apiVersion**|str|APIVersion is the version matched against the api version of the Kafka message. If set, it has to be a string representing a positive integer.<br />If omitted or empty, all versions are allowed.||
|**clientID**|str|ClientID is the client identifier as provided in the request.<br />From Kafka protocol documentation: This is a user supplied identifier for the client application. The user can use any identifier they like and it will be used when logging errors, monitoring aggregates, etc. For example, one might want to monitor not just the requests per second overall, but the number coming from each client application (each of which could reside on multiple servers). This id acts as a logical grouping across all requests from a particular client.<br />If omitted or empty, all client identifiers are allowed.||
|**role**|"produce" \| "consume"|Role is a case-insensitive string and describes a group of API keys necessary to perform certain higher-level Kafka operations such as "produce" or "consume". A Role automatically expands into all APIKeys required to perform the specified higher-level operation.<br />The following values are supported: - "produce": Allow producing to the topics specified in the rule - "consume": Allow consuming from the topics specified in the rule<br />This field is incompatible with the APIKey field, i.e APIKey and Role cannot both be specified in the same rule.<br />If omitted or empty, and if APIKey is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**topic**|str|Topic is the topic name contained in the message. If a Kafka request contains multiple topics, then all topics must be allowed or the message will be rejected.<br />This constraint is ignored if the matched request message type doesn&#39;t contain any topic. Maximum size of Topic can be 249 characters as per recent Kafka spec and allowed characters are a-z, A-Z, 0-9, -, . and _.<br />Older Kafka versions had longer topic lengths of 255, but in Kafka 0.10 version the length was changed from 255 to 249. For compatibility reasons we are using 255.<br />If omitted or empty, all topics are allowed.||

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EnableDefaultDeny

EnableDefaultDeny determines whether this policy configures the subject endpoint(s) to have a default deny mode. If enabled, this causes all traffic not explicitly allowed by a network policy to be dropped. If not specified, the default is true for each traffic direction that has rules, and false otherwise. For example, if a policy only has Ingress or IngressDeny rules, then the default for ingress is true and egress is false. If multiple policies apply to an endpoint, that endpoint&#39;s default deny will be enabled if any policy requests it. This is useful for creating broad-based network policies that will not cause endpoints to enter default-deny mode.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**egress**|bool|Whether or not the endpoint should have a default-deny rule applied to egress traffic.||
|**ingress**|bool|Whether or not the endpoint should have a default-deny rule applied to ingress traffic.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EndpointSelector

EndpointSelector selects all endpoints which should be subject to this rule. EndpointSelector and NodeSelector cannot be both empty and are mutually exclusive.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchExpressions**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EndpointSelectorMatchExpressionsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0endpointselectormatchexpressionsitems0)]|matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0EndpointSelectorMatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0

IngressDenyRule contains all rule types which can be applied at ingress, i.e. network traffic that originates outside of the endpoint and is entering the endpoint selected by the endpointSelector. - All members of this structure are optional. If omitted or empty, the member will have no effect on the rule. - If multiple members are set, all of them need to match in order for the rule to take effect. The exception to this rule is FromRequires field; the effects of any Requires field in any rule will apply to all other rules as well. - FromEndpoints, FromCIDR, FromCIDRSet, FromGroups and FromEntities are mutually exclusive. Only one of these members may be present within an individual rule.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**fromCIDR**|[str]|FromCIDR is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from. Only connections which do *not* originate from the cluster or from the local host are subject to CIDR rules. In order to allow in-cluster connectivity, use the FromEndpoints field.  This will match on the source IP address of incoming connections. Adding  a prefix into FromCIDR or into FromCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is  equivalent.  Overlaps are allowed between FromCIDR and FromCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=my-legacy-pet" is allowed to receive connections from 10.3.9.1||
|**fromCIDRSet**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromCIDRSetItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0fromcidrsetitems0)]|FromCIDRSet is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from in addition to FromEndpoints, along with a list of subnets contained within their corresponding IP block from which traffic should not be allowed. This will match on the source IP address of incoming connections. Adding a prefix into FromCIDR or into FromCIDRSet with no ExcludeCIDRs is equivalent. Overlaps are allowed between FromCIDR and FromCIDRSet.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=my-legacy-pet" is allowed to receive connections from 10.0.0.0/8 except from IPs in subnet 10.96.0.0/12.||
|**fromEndpoints**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromEndpointsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0fromendpointsitems0)]|FromEndpoints is a list of endpoints identified by an EndpointSelector which are allowed to communicate with the endpoint subject to the rule.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "role=backend" can be consumed by any endpoint carrying the label "role=frontend".||
|**fromEntities**|[str]|FromEntities is a list of special entities which the endpoint subject to the rule is allowed to receive connections from. Supported entities are `world`, `cluster` and `host`||
|**fromGroups**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromGroupsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0fromgroupsitems0)]|FromGroups is a directive that allows the integration with multiple outside providers. Currently, only AWS is supported, and the rule can select by multiple sub directives:<br />Example: FromGroups: - aws: securityGroupsIds: - &#39;sg-XXXXXXXXXXXXX&#39;||
|**fromNodes**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromNodesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0fromnodesitems0)]|FromNodes is a list of nodes identified by an EndpointSelector which are allowed to communicate with the endpoint subject to the rule.||
|**fromRequires**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromRequiresItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0fromrequiresitems0)]|FromRequires is a list of additional constraints which must be met in order for the selected endpoints to be reachable. These additional constraints do no by itself grant access privileges and must always be accompanied with at least one matching FromEndpoints.<br />Example: Any Endpoint with the label "team=A" requires consuming endpoint to also carry the label "team=A".||
|**icmps**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0IcmpsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0icmpsitems0)]|ICMPs is a list of ICMP rule identified by type number which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can not accept incoming type 8 ICMP connections.||
|**toPorts**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0ToPortsItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressdenyitems0toportsitems0)]|ToPorts is a list of destination ports identified by port number and protocol which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to receive connections on.<br />Example: Any endpoint with the label "app=httpd" can not accept incoming connections on port 80/tcp.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressDenyItems0FromCIDRSetItems0

CIDRRule is a rule that specifies a CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication  is allowed, along with an optional list of subnets within that CIDR prefix to/from which outside communication is not allowed.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**cidr**|str|CIDR is a CIDR prefix / IP Block.||
|**cidrGroupRef**|str|CIDRGroupRef is a reference to a CiliumCIDRGroup object. A CiliumCIDRGroup contains a list of CIDRs that the endpoint, subject to the rule, can (Ingress/Egress) or cannot (IngressDeny/EgressDeny) receive connections from.||
|**except**|[str]|ExceptCIDRs is a list of IP blocks which the endpoint subject to the rule is not allowed to initiate connections to. These CIDR prefixes should be contained within Cidr, using ExceptCIDRs together with CIDRGroupRef is not supported yet. These exceptions are only applied to the Cidr in this CIDRRule, and do not apply to any other CIDR prefixes in any other CIDRRules.||

The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||

The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0FromRequiresItems0MatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLS

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0OriginatingTLSSecret

Secret is the secret that contains the certificates and private key for the TLS context. By default, Cilium will search in this secret for the following items: - &#39;ca.crt&#39;  - Which represents the trusted CA to verify remote source. - &#39;tls.crt&#39; - Which represents the public key certificate. - &#39;tls.key&#39; - Which represents the private key matching the public key certificate.

### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesDNSItems0

PortRuleDNS is a list of allowed DNS lookups.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchName**|str|MatchName matches literal DNS names. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.||
|**matchPattern**|str|MatchPattern allows using wildcards to match DNS names. All wildcards are case insensitive. The wildcards are: - "*" matches 0 or more DNS valid characters, and may occur anywhere in the pattern. As a special case a "*" as the leftmost character, without a following "." matches all subdomains as well as the name to the right. A trailing "." is automatically added when missing.<br />Examples: `*.cilium.io` matches subomains of cilium at that level www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io match, cilium.io and google.com do not `*cilium.io` matches cilium.io and all subdomains ends with "cilium.io" except those containing "." separator, subcilium.io and sub-cilium.io match, www.cilium.io and blog.cilium.io does not sub*.cilium.io matches subdomains of cilium where the subdomain component begins with "sub" sub.cilium.io and subdomain.cilium.io match, www.cilium.io, blog.cilium.io, cilium.io and google.com do not||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0

PortRuleHTTP is a list of HTTP protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule does not have any effect. All fields of this type are extended POSIX regex as defined by IEEE Std 1003.1, (i.e this follows the egrep/unix syntax, not the perl syntax) matched against the path of an incoming request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**headerMatches**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0)]|HeaderMatches is a list of HTTP headers which must be present and match against the given values. Mismatch field can be used to specify what to do when there is no match.||
|**headers**|[str]|Headers is a list of HTTP headers which must be present in the request. If omitted or empty, requests are allowed regardless of headers present.||
|**host**|str|Host is an extended POSIX regex matched against the host header of a request, e.g. "foo.com"<br />If omitted or empty, the value of the host header is ignored.||
|**method**|str|Method is an extended POSIX regex matched against the method of a request, e.g. "GET", "POST", "PUT", "PATCH", "DELETE", ...<br />If omitted or empty, all methods are allowed.||
|**path**|str|Path is an extended POSIX regex matched against the path of a request. Currently it can contain characters disallowed from the conventional "path" part of a URL as defined by RFC 3986.<br />If omitted or empty, all paths are all allowed.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0

HeaderMatch extends the HeaderValue for matching requirement of a named header field against an immediate string, a secret value, or a regex.  If none of the optional fields is present, then the header value is not matched, only presence of the header is enough.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**mismatch**|"LOG" \| "ADD" \| "DELETE" \| "REPLACE"|Mismatch identifies what to do in case there is no match. The default is to drop the request. Otherwise the overall rule is still considered as matching, but the mismatches are logged in the access log.||
|**name** `required`|str|Name identifies the header.||
|**secret**|[CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret](#ciliumiov2ciliumnetworkpolicyspecsitems0ingressitems0toportsitems0ruleshttpitems0headermatchesitems0secret)|secret||
|**value**|str|Value matches the exact value of the header. Can be specified either alone or together with "Secret"; will be used as the header value if the secret can not be found in the latter case.||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesHTTPItems0HeaderMatchesItems0Secret

Secret refers to a secret that contains the value to be matched against. The secret must only contain one entry. If the referred secret does not exist, and there is no "Value" specified, the match will fail.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**name** `required`|str|Name is the name of the secret.||
|**namespace**|str|Namespace is the namespace in which the secret exists. Context of use determines the default value if left out (e.g., "default").||
### CiliumIoV2CiliumNetworkPolicySpecsItems0IngressItems0ToPortsItems0RulesKafkaItems0

PortRule is a list of Kafka protocol constraints. All fields are optional, if all fields are empty or missing, the rule will match all Kafka messages.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**apiKey**|str|APIKey is a case-insensitive string matched against the key of a request, e.g. "produce", "fetch", "createtopic", "deletetopic", et al Reference: https://kafka.apache.org/protocol#protocol_api_keys<br />If omitted or empty, and if Role is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**apiVersion**|str|APIVersion is the version matched against the api version of the Kafka message. If set, it has to be a string representing a positive integer.<br />If omitted or empty, all versions are allowed.||
|**clientID**|str|ClientID is the client identifier as provided in the request.<br />From Kafka protocol documentation: This is a user supplied identifier for the client application. The user can use any identifier they like and it will be used when logging errors, monitoring aggregates, etc. For example, one might want to monitor not just the requests per second overall, but the number coming from each client application (each of which could reside on multiple servers). This id acts as a logical grouping across all requests from a particular client.<br />If omitted or empty, all client identifiers are allowed.||
|**role**|"produce" \| "consume"|Role is a case-insensitive string and describes a group of API keys necessary to perform certain higher-level Kafka operations such as "produce" or "consume". A Role automatically expands into all APIKeys required to perform the specified higher-level operation.<br />The following values are supported: - "produce": Allow producing to the topics specified in the rule - "consume": Allow consuming from the topics specified in the rule<br />This field is incompatible with the APIKey field, i.e APIKey and Role cannot both be specified in the same rule.<br />If omitted or empty, and if APIKey is not specified, then all keys are allowed.||
|**topic**|str|Topic is the topic name contained in the message. If a Kafka request contains multiple topics, then all topics must be allowed or the message will be rejected.<br />This constraint is ignored if the matched request message type doesn&#39;t contain any topic. Maximum size of Topic can be 249 characters as per recent Kafka spec and allowed characters are a-z, A-Z, 0-9, -, . and _.<br />Older Kafka versions had longer topic lengths of 255, but in Kafka 0.10 version the length was changed from 255 to 249. For compatibility reasons we are using 255.<br />If omitted or empty, all topics are allowed.||

|**requested**|[[CiliumIoV2CiliumNodeSpecIpamPoolsRequestedItems0](#ciliumiov2ciliumnodespecipampoolsrequesteditems0)]|Requested contains a list of IPAM pool requests, i.e. indicates how many addresses this node requests out of each pool listed here. ### CiliumIoV2CiliumNodeSpecIpamPoolsRequestedItems0Needed

Needed indicates how many IPs out of the above Pool this node requests from the operator. The operator runs a reconciliation loop to ensure each node always has enough PodCIDRs allocated in each pool to fulfill the requested number of IPs here.

### CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverride

CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverride specifies configuration overrides for a CiliumBGPNodeConfig. It allows fine-tuning of BGP behavior on a per-node basis. For the override to be effective, the names in CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverride and CiliumBGPNodeConfig must match exactly. This matching ensures that specific node configurations are applied correctly and only where intended.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**apiVersion** `required` `readOnly`|"cilium.io/v2alpha1"|APIVersion defines the versioned schema of this representation of an object. Servers should convert recognized schemas to the latest internal value, and may reject unrecognized values. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#resources|"cilium.io/v2alpha1"|
|**kind** `required` `readOnly`|"CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverride"|Kind is a string value representing the REST resource this object represents. Servers may infer this from the endpoint the client submits requests to. Cannot be updated. In CamelCase. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#types-kinds|"CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverride"|
|**metadata** `required`|[ObjectMeta](#objectmeta)|metadata||
|**spec** `required`|[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPNodeConfigOverrideSpec](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpnodeconfigoverridespec)|spec||

### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0

BGPAdvertisement defines which routes Cilium should advertise to BGP peers. Optionally, additional attributes can be set to the advertised routes.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**advertisementType** `required`|"PodCIDR" \| "CiliumPodIPPool" \| "Service"|AdvertisementType defines type of advertisement which has to be advertised.||
|**attributes**|[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0Attributes](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpadvertisementspecadvertisementsitems0attributes)|attributes||
|**selector**|[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0Selector](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpadvertisementspecadvertisementsitems0selector)|selector||
|**service**|[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0Service](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpadvertisementspecadvertisementsitems0service)|service||
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0Attributes

Attributes defines additional attributes to set to the advertised routes. If not specified, no additional attributes are set.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**communities**|[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0AttributesCommunities](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpadvertisementspecadvertisementsitems0attributescommunities)|communities||
|**localPreference**|int|LocalPreference sets the local preference attribute in the route. If not specified, no local preference attribute is set.||
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0AttributesCommunities

Communities sets the community attributes in the route. If not specified, no community attribute is set.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**large**|[str]|Large holds a list of the BGP Large Communities Attribute (RFC 8092) values.||
|**standard**|[str]|Standard holds a list of "standard" 32-bit BGP Communities Attribute (RFC 1997) values defined as numeric values.||
|**wellKnown**|[str]|WellKnown holds a list "standard" 32-bit BGP Communities Attribute (RFC 1997) values defined as well-known string aliases to their numeric values.||
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0Selector

Selector is a label selector to select objects of the type specified by AdvertisementType. If not specified, all objects of the type specified by AdvertisementType are selected for advertisement.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**matchExpressions**|[[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0SelectorMatchExpressionsItems0](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumbgpadvertisementspecadvertisementsitems0selectormatchexpressionsitems0)]|matchExpressions is a list of label selector requirements. The requirements are ANDed.||
|**matchLabels**|{str:str}|matchLabels is a map of {key,value} pairs. A single {key,value} in the matchLabels map is equivalent to an element of matchExpressions, whose key field is "key", the operator is "In", and the values array contains only "value". The requirements are ANDed.||
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPAdvertisementSpecAdvertisementsItems0SelectorMatchExpressionsItems0

A label selector requirement is a selector that contains values, a key, and an operator that relates the key and values.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**key** `required`|str|key is the label key that the selector applies to.||
|**operator** `required`|"In" \| "NotIn" \| "Exists" \| "DoesNotExist"|operator represents a key&#39;s relationship to a set of values. Valid operators are In, NotIn, Exists and DoesNotExist.||
|**values**|[str]|values is an array of string values. If the operator is In or NotIn, the values array must be non-empty. If the operator is Exists or DoesNotExist, the values array must be empty. This array is replaced during a strategic merge patch.||

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**addresses**|[str]|Addresses is a list of service address types which needs to be advertised via BGP.||

### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPPeerConfigSpecGracefulRestart

GracefulRestart defines graceful restart parameters which are negotiated with this peer. If not specified, the graceful restart capability is disabled.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**enabled** `required`|bool|Enabled flag, when set enables graceful restart capability.||
|**restartTimeSeconds**|int|RestartTimeSeconds is the estimated time it will take for the BGP session to be re-established with peer after a restart. After this period, peer will remove stale routes. This is described RFC 4724 section 4.2.|120|
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPPeerConfigSpecTimers

Timers defines the BGP timers for the peer. If not specified, the default timers are used.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**connectRetryTimeSeconds**|int|ConnectRetryTimeSeconds defines the initial value for the BGP ConnectRetryTimer (RFC 4271, Section 8).<br />If not specified, defaults to 120 seconds.|120|
|**holdTimeSeconds**|int|HoldTimeSeconds defines the initial value for the BGP HoldTimer (RFC 4271, Section 4.2). Updating this value will cause a session reset.<br />If not specified, defaults to 90 seconds.|90|
|**keepAliveTimeSeconds**|int|KeepaliveTimeSeconds defines the initial value for the BGP KeepaliveTimer (RFC 4271, Section 8). It can not be larger than HoldTimeSeconds. Updating this value will cause a session reset.<br />If not specified, defaults to 30 seconds.|30|
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumBGPPeerConfigSpecTransport

Transport defines the BGP transport parameters for the peer. If not specified, the default transport parameters are used.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**localPort**|int|Deprecated LocalPort is the local port to be used for the BGP session.<br />If not specified, ephemeral port will be picked to initiate a connection.<br />This field is deprecated and will be removed in a future release. Local port configuration is unnecessary and is not recommended.||
|**peerPort**|int|PeerPort is the peer port to be used for the BGP session.<br />If not specified, defaults to TCP port 179.|179|

### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumL2AnnouncementPolicyStatusConditionsItems0

Condition contains details for one aspect of the current state of this API Resource. --- This struct is intended for direct use as an array at the field path .status.conditions.  For example, type FooStatus struct{ // Represents the observations of a foo&#39;s current state. // Known .status.conditions.type are: "Available", "Progressing", and "Degraded" // +patchMergeKey=type // +patchStrategy=merge // +listType=map // +listMapKey=type Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type" protobuf:"bytes,1,rep,name=conditions"` // other fields }

|**lastTransitionTime** `required`|str|lastTransitionTime is the last time the condition transitioned from one status to another. This should be when the underlying condition changed.  If that is not known, then using the time when the API field changed is acceptable.||
|**message** `required`|str|message is a human readable message indicating details about the transition. This may be an empty string.||
|**observedGeneration**|int|observedGeneration represents the .metadata.generation that the condition was set based upon. For instance, if .metadata.generation is currently 12, but the .status.conditions[x].observedGeneration is 9, the condition is out of date with respect to the current state of the instance.||
|**reason** `required`|str|reason contains a programmatic identifier indicating the reason for the condition&#39;s last transition. Producers of specific condition types may define expected values and meanings for this field, and whether the values are considered a guaranteed API. The value should be a CamelCase string. This field may not be empty.||
|**status** `required`|"True" \| "False" \| "Unknown"|status of the condition, one of True, False, Unknown.||
|**type** `required`|str|||
### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumLoadBalancerIPPoolSpec

Spec is a human readable description for a BGP load balancer ip pool.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowFirstLastIPs**|"Yes" \| "No"|AllowFirstLastIPs, if set to `yes` means that the first and last IPs of each CIDR will be allocatable. If `no` or undefined, these IPs will be reserved. This field is ignored for /{31,32} and /{127,128} CIDRs since reserving the first and last IPs would make the CIDRs unusable.||
|**blocks**|[[CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumLoadBalancerIPPoolSpecBlocksItems0](#ciliumiov2alpha1ciliumloadbalancerippoolspecblocksitems0)]|Blocks is a list of CIDRs comprising this IP Pool||
|**disabled**|bool|Disabled, if set to true means that no new IPs will be allocated from this pool. Existing allocations will not be removed from services.|False|

### CiliumIoV2alpha1CiliumLoadBalancerIPPoolStatus

Status is the status of the IP Pool. It might be possible for users to define overlapping IP Pools, we can&#39;t validate or enforce non-overlapping pools during object creation. The Cilium operator will do this validation and update the status to reflect the ability to allocate IPs from this pool.
